They wrap it in a content-addressed JSON \"pack\" (schema_version=1, single `files.SKILL.md` entry, ≤32,768 bytes), upload it to any HTTP endpoint, and commit `{sha256}|{url}` on-chain. No GPU, server, or uptime is required.\n\n**Scoring (reward function).** Each epoch the validator:\n1. Reads the on-chain commitment, fetches the pack, and verifies its SHA256 matches.\n2. Runs the agent (Hermes) inside each scenario's Terminal-Bench container, with `SKILL.md` + the scenario's `INSTRUCTION.md` as input.\n3. Spins up a fresh verifier container that runs `pytest` and produces `ctrf.json`; per-scenario **quality = passed_tests / total_tests** (continuous in [0,1]).\n4. Runs multiple episodes per scenario and computes (`_SessionResult.compute_scores`):\n - `mean_quality` across episodes\n - `early_mean` (ep 0–1) and `late_mean` (ep 2–3)\n - `delta = late_mean − early_mean`\n - `learning_bonus` derived from delta (rewards skills that improve as the agent gains experience)\n - `final_score` = combination of mean quality + learning bonus\n5. The final per-miner score is the equal-weighted sum across all scenarios. Cost (USD) is tracked as a separate axis, not as a score input.\n\n**Maximizing emissions.** Bittensor weights here are **winner-take-all** — only the top-scoring miner gets ~100% of subnet rewards. To win:\n- Write a *general-purpose* SKILL.md that lifts performance across many heterogeneous scenarios (you don't know which scenarios the validator will run, and Season 2 adds new auto-generated ones).\n- Maximize `pytest` pass rates inside the actual sandbox containers (not just LLM-judged quality).\n- Encourage strategies that let the agent improve across episodes (positive delta → learning bonus).\n- Be a **first mover** — there's an anti-copy mechanism: NCD (normalized compression distance) similarity detection plus a first-mover threshold, so duplicating a winning pack won't displace the original.\n\n**Penalties / skip conditions.**\n- **Hash mismatch / unfetchable pack / invalid schema** → pack rejected, no score (`PackFetcher.verify_submission` must return valid=True; schema is validated via `validate_s1`).\n- **Pack > 32 KB, missing/empty SKILL.md, wrong schema_version** → validation fails, no score.\n- **Provider failure** (Hermes exits non-zero on every scenario, no agent output, $0 cost) → `SKIP_PROVIDER_FAILURE` — the eval is discarded rather than submitted as a zero, so transient LLM outages don't poison a miner.\n- **Inactivity** (`INACTIVITY_BLOCKS`, default ~48h with no fresh commitment) → miner is treated as inactive.\n- **NCD similarity above `SIMILARITY_THRESHOLD`** (default 0.80) to an earlier pack → flagged as a copy; first-mover keeps the score.","reward_summary_short":"Miners are rewarded for writing a single `SKILL.md` instruction file (≤32 KB) that teaches an AI agent (Hermes) how to solve real Terminal-Bench-style operational scenarios. Otherwise:\n\n```\nttft_imp = max(0, (baseline_ttft - miner_ttft) / baseline_ttft)\ntps_imp = max(0, (miner_tps - baseline_tps) / baseline_tps)\nscore = 0.5 * ttft_imp + 0.5 * tps_imp\n```\n\nSo score is a 50/50 blend of time-to-first-token improvement and throughput (tokens/sec) improvement over baseline, each clamped at zero (you can't be penalized for being slower than vLLM, but you get no credit either).\n\n**Emission distribution.** This is a winner-take-most competition, not a continuous leaderboard. The total pool size scales with the winner's score relative to a target improvement — so the subnet emits more when the winner is meaningfully better than baseline, less when improvements are marginal. To submit a new attempt, you need a freshly registered hotkey.\n- **No improvement → no reward:** clamping at zero means matching or losing to the baseline contributes nothing, and you only earn emissions if you're #1 or #2 overall.\n- **1% challenge margin:** beating the winner by a hair (sub-1%) doesn't take the crown — protects incumbents from measurement noise.","reward_summary_short":"Cacheon (SN14) rewards miners for building the fastest correct LLM inference server for `Qwen2.5-72B-Instruct` on 8-GPU pods. It then computes outlier-resistant normalized components against the network's P95:\n\n- `sales_norm = min(1, √sales / √P95_sales)` — square-root compression rewards volume but caps whales\n- `rev_norm = min(1, ln(1+rev) / ln(1+P95_rev))` — log compression rewards revenue, fair to high-ticket sales\n- `base = 0.15 · sales_norm + 0.85 · rev_norm` — revenue dominates by design (merchant value)\n- `ref = min(1, refund_orders / max(1, sales))`\n- **`score = base · (1 − ref)`** — refunds act as a multiplicative penalty\n\nScores are converted to weights, optionally have a per-campaign \"creator burn\" portion redirected to the subnet owner, and set on-chain. Miners with zero sales get zero score; miners with only pending (not-yet-verified) orders get a small `PENDING_MINER_MIN_SCORE` so they aren't deregistered.\n\n**3. How to maximize emissions**\n- Drive **high USD revenue** — it's 85% of the base score, and log-normalization means revenue per sale matters a lot.\n- Maintain meaningful **sales volume** (15% weight, sqrt-normalized, so the first sales matter most; an optional <3-sales soft cap can apply 30% credit).\n- Target campaigns where you can approach (but don't need to exceed) the P95 thresholds — going past P95 gives no extra credit.\n- Keep refunds/chargebacks low — a 25% refund rate is a flat 25% score cut.\n\n**4. Penalties / slashing**\nThere's no on-chain slashing of stake, but score is suppressed by: refunds (multiplicative `1 − refund_rate`), unverified sales (only webhook-confirmed orders count), and zero sales → zero score. Subnet-wide, a **burn mechanism** redirects emissions to the owner when emitted ALPHA value exceeds verified sales value, preventing miner over-profitability and sell pressure on ALPHA.","reward_summary_short":"BitAds (SN16) rewards miners for driving verified sales to advertiser campaigns — miners promote BitAds campaigns on any platform they choose and earn based on webhook-verified orders and USD revenue over a rolling 30-day window. The miner must split the document into chunks and return them. The goal is to produce chunks that are useful as retrieval units in a RAG system — each chunk should be internally coherent (one topic) and distinct from other chunks.\n\n**Scoring (reward function).** The validator evaluates returned chunks using an embedding-based semantic metric. Roughly:\n\n1. **Embed sentences** in each chunk using a sentence embedding model.\n2. **Intra-chunk similarity** — sample sentence pairs *within* the same chunk and compute cosine similarity. Higher is better (chunks should be topically tight).\n3. **Inter-chunk dissimilarity** — sample sentence pairs *across different* chunks and compute cosine similarity. Lower is better (chunks should not overlap topically).\n4. The raw score combines these: reward ∝ (intra-chunk similarity − inter-chunk similarity), typically as an expected-value comparison over many sampled pairs.\n5. **Tournament/ranking step.** Miners are grouped and ranked against each other on the same input; emissions follow the ranking rather than absolute scores, so miners compete head-to-head per query.\n6. **Latency tiebreak.** Faster valid responses are preferred when quality is comparable.\n\n**What maximizes emissions.**\n- Respecting `chunk_size` exactly — chunks must stay under the byte/token cap.\n- Splitting on true semantic boundaries (paragraph/topic shifts), not arbitrary fixed-window cuts.\n- Producing the requested number of chunks (`chunk_qty`); deviations are penalized.\n- Returning quickly within the timeout.\n- Using an embedding-aware chunker (e.g., semantic splitters that look at sentence-embedding distance to find boundaries) rather than naive character/word splitters.\n\n**Penalties / disqualification.**\n- **Hard size violations** — any chunk exceeding `chunk_size` zeros out (or massively penalizes) the response.\n- **Excessive cross-chunk overlap** — duplicating sentences across chunks is detected and penalized; chunks must be a near-partition of the source.\n- **Timeouts / no response** — score of 0 for that round.\n- **Returning the raw document unchanged** or trivial splits — caught by the inter-chunk similarity metric (high overlap → low score).\n- Persistent low ranking in the tournament leads to deregistration over time as stake/emissions decay.\n\nNote: the GitHub fetch returned 404, so this is based on the published design of VectorChat's Chunking subnet rather than the exact current code. The output is a full predictive distribution at each timestep, not a single point forecast.\n\n2. **Scoring metric** — Validators wait for the horizon to elapse, fetch the realized price series from a reference data source, and score each miner's submitted ensemble using a proper scoring rule — Synth uses **CRPS (Continuous Ranked Probability Score)**, often aggregated across multiple time deltas (e.g. 5m, 30m, 3h, 24h ahead). CRPS simultaneously penalizes (a) bias (the mean of the distribution being far from the realized price), (b) miscalibration (the realized price falling in low-density regions of the predicted distribution), and (c) excessive vagueness (very wide distributions are penalized even when they cover the truth). Per-horizon CRPS values are normalized/ranked across miners and combined into a single reward score, which feeds the validator's weight vector.\n\n3. **Behaviors that maximize emissions**:\n - Producing well-calibrated, *sharp* distributions — tight enough to be informative, wide enough to actually cover realized outcomes.\n - Modeling volatility regimes accurately, not just the mean trajectory (since CRPS punishes both under- and over-dispersion).\n - Responding to fresh market state on every forecast request — stale or generic priors get beaten by competitors who incorporate live order-book / volatility signals.\n - Reliably responding to validator queries on time; missed or malformed submissions score as worst-case.\n\n4. **Penalties / slashing**:\n - Late, missing, or malformed submissions receive a maximum-penalty CRPS (effectively zero reward for that round).\n - Submissions that fail structural checks (wrong number of paths, wrong horizon, non-monotonic timestamps, NaNs) are rejected.\n - Detected duplication / copying from other miners is filtered out before scoring in many Bittensor subnets; Synth's validator includes anti-collusion / similarity checks so near-identical ensembles across UIDs get suppressed.\n - There is no on-chain stake slashing beyond Bittensor's standard mechanics — \"punishment\" is via zero/low weights, which starve the miner of emissions.\n\nIf you want, I can retry fetching the repo to confirm the exact CRPS weighting, horizon list, and any recent changes to the reward function — the 301 suggests the URL needs a redirect follow.","reward_summary_short":"Synth rewards miners for producing probabilistic price forecasts of crypto assets (primarily BTC) — miners submit many simulated future price paths over short horizons, and validators score the calibration/accuracy of those distributions against realized prices. They mutate opcodes, addresses, and constants over up to ~150 generations on a fixed CIFAR-10 binary task suite (deterministically seeded so every genome is scored on the same tasks). Two participation modes exist: **Direct Mining** (solo, larger reward) and **Pool Mining** (collaborative, where the pool computes a median consensus with 10% tolerance across ≥3 evaluators and submits on behalf of participants). Scoring / reward function**\nThe flow is:\n- Miner evolves locally until its algorithm's verified score exceeds the current SOTA threshold (cached for ~30s via `sota_cache_seconds`).\n- It submits to the relay (`relay.bitsota.com`); validators download and **independently re-verify** the algorithm via `core.evaluations.verify_solution_quality` on their own task suite (controlled by `validator_task_count`).\n- Validators set on-chain weights in one of two modes:\n - **Relay mode** — wait for relay/multi-sig consensus before setting weights.\n - **Local mode** — set weights immediately from own evaluation.\n- The weight distribution is hard-coded: **90% burn, 10% to the winning miner.** Emissions then flow via Yuma consensus.\n\nSo the \"score\" is effectively a verified accuracy/fitness number on the CIFAR-10 binary task, and rewards are **winner-take-all per SOTA break** rather than a continuous distribution.\n\n**3. The validator pulls prompts from a battery of programmatically generated, auto-verifiable environments — Affine's canonical set includes SAT (boolean satisfiability), ABDUCTION, and DEDUCTION, with the environment list expandable. Each prompt has a deterministic correctness check, so scoring is grader-free and cheap.\n\n2. **Scoring / reward function.** For every (miner, environment) pair the validator computes an accuracy score over a rolling sample of challenges. Rewards are NOT a simple weighted sum of accuracies — Affine's signature mechanism is **Pareto dominance**: a miner earns emission only if no other miner Pareto-dominates them across the full environment vector. Among non-dominated miners, weight is concentrated on those that win (or tie for best) on at least one environment, typically with a winner-take-most curve per environment. This means being mediocre everywhere pays nothing; being SOTA on even one environment pays.\n\n3. **Behaviors that maximize emissions.**\n - Submit a model that is *best-in-class* on at least one environment while remaining competitive on the others (avoiding domination).\n - Keep the inference endpoint highly available — unreachable or slow miners get zero-scored on queried challenges.\n - Track which environments are under-served and specialize there (lower competition → easier frontier).\n - Continuously upgrade: the validator re-samples, so stale models get displaced as soon as a new miner ties+beats them on any axis.\n\n4. **Penalties / slashing.** No on-chain slashing in the Yuma sense, but effective penalties include: (a) any miner Pareto-dominated by another receives ~zero weight, (b) endpoint failures, timeouts, or malformed outputs count as wrong answers and tank that environment's score, (c) detected cheating (hard-coded answers, identical-model duplication via copy-mining) is filtered by the validator's de-duplication / lookup-based grading. (Poker44) is a poker bot detection subnet. Miners develop machine learning models that classify poker hand histories as either human-played or bot-played. Validators query miners with batches of poker hand data and score their detection accuracy.\n\nTask Miners Perform:\nMiners receive DetectionSynapse(chunks=[...]) payloads where each chunk is a list of poker hand dictionaries. For each chunk, miners must return a single risk_score (float between 0 and 1) indicating the probability that the chunk is bot-played (1=bot, 0=human). Miners process multiple chunks per forward cycle and must return one score per chunk. The evaluation data is produced by Poker44 platform infrastructure from canonical live tables.\n\nScoring Function Mechanics:\nThe reward function (poker44/score/scoring.py) computes:\n1. Confusion matrix from rounded predictions vs ground truth labels (0=human, 1=bot).\n2. False Positive Rate (FPR): fp / (tn + fp) - rate of incorrectly flagging humans as bots.\n3. Bot Recall (TPR): tp / (tp + fn) - rate of correctly identifying bots.\n4. Average Precision Score (AP): area under precision-recall curve using raw risk scores.\n5. Human safety penalty: max(0, 1-FPR)^2 — hard penalty for false positives against humans. If FPR >= 0.10, human_safety_penalty = 0.0 (complete zeroing of score).\n6. Base score: 0.65 * ap_score + 0.35 * bot_recall.\n7. Final reward: base_score * human_safety_penalty.\n\nCompetition structure: Rolling 72-hour epochs anchored at 20:00 UTC. Canonical evaluation material refreshed in 6-hour windows. Production validators read the canonical competition weight vector from the backend API (Poker44 platform runtime).
